[{]: <region> (header)
# Step 23: Migration to Angular2
[}]: #
[{]: <region> (body)
In this chapter we will be upgrading Socially from Angular1 to Angular2 using Angular's [Upgrade Adapter](https://angular.io/docs/ts/latest/guide/upgrade.html). Why upgrading? Because Angular2 is the next major version of the framework and it will surely be the version we want to go with when building web apps in the future, and we can enjoy many of its benefits like better performance, server-side rendering, more powerful templating, better ecosystem and more. We will also be transforming our JavaScript code into [TypeScript](https://www.typescriptlang.org/) inspired by Angular2 team's recommendation.

## Switching to TypeScript

First, we will remove the JavaScript compiler, whos belonging Meteor package is `pbastowski:angular-babel`:

    meteor remove pbastowski:angular-babel

Although it is possible to just replace the old JavaScript compiler with a TypeScript compiler, we would like to reserve `ng-annotate`'s compiler as well, since the updating process is gonna be done gradually and our app is gonna be a hybrid of Angular1 and Angular2. Thus, we're gonna install the following package:

    meteor add mys:typescript-ng-annotate

Once our app is fully migrated to Angular2, we will replace `mys:typescript-ng-annotate` with `barbatus:typescript`, a package which will provide you with a pure TypeScript compiler. TypeScript compiler also relies on [declerations](https://www.typescriptlang.org/docs/handbook/declaration-files/introduction.html), which can be installed via package manager called `typings`. Further informations about `typings` and how to install it can be found [here](https://github.com/typings/typings). As for now just add the following configuration files:

[{]: <helper> (diff_step 23.3)

@@ -0,0 +1,2626 @@
+â”Š    â”Š   1â”Š// Generated by typings
+â”Š    â”Š   2â”Š// Source: https://raw.githubusercontent.com/types/env-node/374f42213af406d9f76e9181da371df3f9e93903/6.0/node.d.ts
+â”Š    â”Š   3â”Šinterface NodeError {
+â”Š    â”Š   4â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š   5â”Š   * Returns a string describing the point in the code at which the Error was instantiated.
+â”Š    â”Š   6â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š   7â”Š   * For example:
+â”Š    â”Š   8â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š   9â”Š   * ```
+â”Š    â”Š  10â”Š   * Error: Things keep happening!
+â”Š    â”Š  11â”Š   *    at /home/gbusey/file.js:525:2
+â”Š    â”Š  12â”Š   *    at Frobnicator.refrobulate (/home/gbusey/business-logic.js:424:21)
+â”Š    â”Š  13â”Š   *    at Actor.<anonymous> (/home/gbusey/actors.js:400:8)
+â”Š    â”Š  14â”Š   *    at increaseSynergy (/home/gbusey/actors.js:701:6)
+â”Š    â”Š  15â”Š   * ```
+â”Š    â”Š  16â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š  17â”Š   * The first line is formatted as <error class name>: <error message>, and is followed by a series of stack frames (each line beginning with "at "). Each frame describes a call site within the code that lead to the error being generated. V8 attempts to display a name for each function (by variable name, function name, or object method name), but occasionally it will not be able to find a suitable name. If V8 cannot determine a name for the function, only location information will be displayed for that frame. Otherwise, the determined function name will be displayed with location information appended in parentheses.
+â”Š    â”Š  18â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š  19â”Š  stack?: string;
+â”Š    â”Š  20â”Š
+â”Š    â”Š  21â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š  22â”Š   * Returns the string description of error as set by calling new Error(message). The message passed to the constructor will also appear in the first line of the stack trace of the Error, however changing this property after the Error object is created may not change the first line of the stack trace.
+â”Š    â”Š  23â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š  24â”Š   * ```
+â”Š    â”Š  25â”Š   * const err = new Error('The message');
+â”Š    â”Š  26â”Š   * console.log(err.message);
+â”Š    â”Š  27â”Š   * // Prints: The message
+â”Š    â”Š  28â”Š   * ```
+â”Š    â”Š  29â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š  30â”Š  message: string;
+â”Š    â”Š  31â”Š}
+â”Š    â”Š  32â”Šinterface Error extends NodeError { }
+â”Š    â”Š  33â”Š
+â”Š    â”Š  34â”Šinterface ErrorConstructor {
+â”Š    â”Š  35â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š  36â”Š   * Creates a `.stack` property on `targetObject`, which when accessed returns a string representing the location in the code at which `Error.captureStackTrace()`` was called.
+â”Š    â”Š  37â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š  38â”Š   * ```js
+â”Š    â”Š  39â”Š   * const myObject = {};
+â”Š    â”Š  40â”Š   * Error.captureStackTrace(myObject);
+â”Š    â”Š  41â”Š   * myObject.stack  // similar to `new Error().stack`
+â”Š    â”Š  42â”Š   * ```
+â”Š    â”Š  43â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š  44â”Š   * The first line of the trace, instead of being prefixed with `ErrorType : message`, will be the result of calling `targetObject.toString()``.
+â”Š    â”Š  45â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š  46â”Š   * The optional constructorOpt argument accepts a function. If given, all frames above constructorOpt, including constructorOpt, will be omitted from the generated stack trace.
+â”Š    â”Š  47â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š  48â”Š   * The constructorOpt argument is useful for hiding implementation details of error generation from an end user. For instance:
+â”Š    â”Š  49â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š  50â”Š   * ```js
+â”Š    â”Š  51â”Š   * function MyError() {
+â”Š    â”Š  52â”Š   *   Error.captureStackTrace(this, MyError);
+â”Š    â”Š  53â”Š   * }
+â”Š    â”Š  54â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š  55â”Š   * // Without passing MyError to captureStackTrace, the MyError
+â”Š    â”Š  56â”Š   * // frame would should up in the .stack property. by passing
+â”Š    â”Š  57â”Š   * // the constructor, we omit that frame and all frames above it.
+â”Š    â”Š  58â”Š   * new MyError().stack
+â”Š    â”Š  59â”Š   * ```
+â”Š    â”Š  60â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š  61â”Š  captureStackTrace<T extends { stack?: string }>(targetObject: T, constructorOpt?: new () => T): void;
+â”Š    â”Š  62â”Š
+â”Š    â”Š  63â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š  64â”Š   * The Error.stackTraceLimit property specifies the number of stack frames collected by a stack trace (whether generated by `new Error().stack` or `Error.captureStackTrace(obj))``.
+â”Š    â”Š  65â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š  66â”Š   * The default value is 10 but may be set to any valid JavaScript number. Changes will affect any stack trace captured after the value has been changed.
+â”Š    â”Š  67â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š  68â”Š   * If set to a non-number value, or set to a negative number, stack traces will not capture any frames.
+â”Š    â”Š  69â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š  70â”Š  stackTraceLimit: number;
+â”Š    â”Š  71â”Š}

+â”Š    â”Š 243â”Š// Buffer class
+â”Š    â”Š 244â”Štype BufferEncoding = "ascii" | "utf8" | "utf16le" | "ucs2" | "binary" | "hex";
+â”Š    â”Š 245â”Šinterface Buffer extends NodeBuffer { }
+â”Š    â”Š 246â”Š
+â”Š    â”Š 247â”Š/**
+â”Š    â”Š 248â”Š * Raw data is stored in instances of the Buffer class.
+â”Š    â”Š 249â”Š * A Buffer is similar to an array of integers but corresponds to a raw memory allocation outside the V8 heap.  A Buffer cannot be resized.
+â”Š    â”Š 250â”Š * Valid string encodings: 'ascii'|'utf8'|'utf16le'|'ucs2'(alias of 'utf16le')|'base64'|'binary'(deprecated)|'hex'
+â”Š    â”Š 251â”Š */
+â”Š    â”Š 252â”Šdeclare var Buffer: {
+â”Š    â”Š 253â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 254â”Š   * Allocates a new buffer containing the given {str}.
+â”Š    â”Š 255â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 256â”Š   * @param str String to store in buffer.
+â”Š    â”Š 257â”Š   * @param encoding encoding to use, optional.  Default is 'utf8'
+â”Š    â”Š 258â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 259â”Š  new (str: string, encoding?: string): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 260â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 261â”Š   * Allocates a new buffer of {size} octets.
+â”Š    â”Š 262â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 263â”Š   * @param size count of octets to allocate.
+â”Š    â”Š 264â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 265â”Š  new (size: number): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 266â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 267â”Š   * Allocates a new buffer containing the given {array} of octets.
+â”Š    â”Š 268â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 269â”Š   * @param array The octets to store.
+â”Š    â”Š 270â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 271â”Š  new (array: Uint8Array): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 272â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 273â”Š   * Produces a Buffer backed by the same allocated memory as
+â”Š    â”Š 274â”Š   * the given {ArrayBuffer}.
+â”Š    â”Š 275â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 276â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 277â”Š   * @param arrayBuffer The ArrayBuffer with which to share memory.
+â”Š    â”Š 278â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 279â”Š  new (arrayBuffer: ArrayBuffer): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 280â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 281â”Š   * Allocates a new buffer containing the given {array} of octets.
+â”Š    â”Š 282â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 283â”Š   * @param array The octets to store.
+â”Š    â”Š 284â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 285â”Š  new (array: any[]): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 286â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 287â”Š   * Copies the passed {buffer} data onto a new {Buffer} instance.
+â”Š    â”Š 288â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 289â”Š   * @param buffer The buffer to copy.
+â”Š    â”Š 290â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 291â”Š  new (buffer: Buffer): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 292â”Š  prototype: Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 293â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 294â”Š   * Allocates a new Buffer using an {array} of octets.
+â”Š    â”Š 295â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 296â”Š   * @param array
+â”Š    â”Š 297â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 298â”Š  from(array: any[]): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 299â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 300â”Š   * When passed a reference to the .buffer property of a TypedArray instance,
+â”Š    â”Š 301â”Š   * the newly created Buffer will share the same allocated memory as the TypedArray.
+â”Š    â”Š 302â”Š   * The optional {byteOffset} and {length} arguments specify a memory range
+â”Š    â”Š 303â”Š   * within the {arrayBuffer} that will be shared by the Buffer.
+â”Š    â”Š 304â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 305â”Š   * @param arrayBuffer The .buffer property of a TypedArray or a new ArrayBuffer()
+â”Š    â”Š 306â”Š   * @param byteOffset
+â”Š    â”Š 307â”Š   * @param length
+â”Š    â”Š 308â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 309â”Š  from(arrayBuffer: ArrayBuffer, byteOffset?: number, length?: number): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 310â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 311â”Š   * Copies the passed {buffer} data onto a new Buffer instance.
+â”Š    â”Š 312â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 313â”Š   * @param buffer
+â”Š    â”Š 314â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 315â”Š  from(buffer: Buffer): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 316â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 317â”Š   * Allocates a new `Buffer` of `size` bytes. If `fill` is `undefined`, the `Buffer` will be _zero-filled_.
+â”Š    â”Š 318â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 319â”Š   * @param size The desired length of the new `Buffer`
+â”Š    â”Š 320â”Š   * @param fill A value to pre-fill the new `Buffer` with. Default: `0`
+â”Š    â”Š 321â”Š   * @param encoding If `fill` is a string, this is its encoding. Default: `'utf8'`
+â”Š    â”Š 322â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 323â”Š  alloc(size: number, fill?: string | Buffer | number, encoding?: string): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 324â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 325â”Š   * Allocates a new _non-zero-filled_ `Buffer` of `size` bytes. The `size` must be less than or equal to the value of `buffer.kMaxLength`. Otherwise, a `RangeError` is thrown. A zero-length `Buffer` will be created if `size <= 0`.
+â”Š    â”Š 326â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 327â”Š   * The underlying memory for `Buffer` instances created in this way is not initialized. The contents of the newly created `Buffer` are unknown and _may contain sensitive data_. Use `buf.fill(0)` to initialize such `Buffer` instances to zeroes.
+â”Š    â”Š 328â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 329â”Š   * @param size The desired length of the new `Buffer`
+â”Š    â”Š 330â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 331â”Š  allocUnsafe(size: number): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 332â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 333â”Š   * Creates a new Buffer containing the given JavaScript string {str}.
+â”Š    â”Š 334â”Š   * If provided, the {encoding} parameter identifies the character encoding.
+â”Š    â”Š 335â”Š   * If not provided, {encoding} defaults to 'utf8'.
+â”Š    â”Š 336â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 337â”Š   * @param str
+â”Š    â”Š 338â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 339â”Š  from(str: string, encoding?: string): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 340â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 341â”Š   * Returns true if {obj} is a Buffer
+â”Š    â”Š 342â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 343â”Š   * @param obj object to test.
+â”Š    â”Š 344â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 345â”Š  isBuffer(obj: any): obj is Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 346â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 347â”Š   * Returns true if {encoding} is a valid encoding argument.
+â”Š    â”Š 348â”Š   * Valid string encodings in Node 0.12: 'ascii'|'utf8'|'utf16le'|'ucs2'(alias of 'utf16le')|'base64'|'binary'(deprecated)|'hex'
+â”Š    â”Š 349â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 350â”Š   * @param encoding string to test.
+â”Š    â”Š 351â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 352â”Š  isEncoding(encoding: string): boolean;
+â”Š    â”Š 353â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 354â”Š   * Gives the actual byte length of a string. encoding defaults to 'utf8'.
+â”Š    â”Š 355â”Š   * This is not the same as String.prototype.length since that returns the number of characters in a string.
+â”Š    â”Š 356â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 357â”Š   * @param string string to test.
+â”Š    â”Š 358â”Š   * @param encoding encoding used to evaluate (defaults to 'utf8')
+â”Š    â”Š 359â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 360â”Š  byteLength(string: string, encoding?: string): number;
+â”Š    â”Š 361â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 362â”Š   * Returns a buffer which is the result of concatenating all the buffers in the list together.
+â”Š    â”Š 363â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 364â”Š   * If the list has no items, or if the totalLength is 0, then it returns a zero-length buffer.
+â”Š    â”Š 365â”Š   * If the list has exactly one item, then the first item of the list is returned.
+â”Š    â”Š 366â”Š   * If the list has more than one item, then a new Buffer is created.
+â”Š    â”Š 367â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š 368â”Š   * @param list An array of Buffer objects to concatenate
+â”Š    â”Š 369â”Š   * @param totalLength Total length of the buffers when concatenated.
+â”Š    â”Š 370â”Š   *   If totalLength is not provided, it is read from the buffers in the list. However, this adds an additional loop to the function, so it is faster to provide the length explicitly.
+â”Š    â”Š 371â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 372â”Š  concat(list: Buffer[], totalLength?: number): Buffer;
+â”Š    â”Š 373â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š 374â”Š   * The same as buf1.compare(buf2).
+â”Š    â”Š 375â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š 376â”Š  compare(buf1: Buffer, buf2: Buffer): number;
+â”Š    â”Š 377â”Š};

+â”Š    â”Š1872â”Š  export interface ParsedPath {
+â”Š    â”Š1873â”Š    /**
+â”Š    â”Š1874â”Š     * The root of the path such as '/' or 'c:\'
+â”Š    â”Š1875â”Š     */

+â”Š    â”Š1877â”Š    /**

+â”Š    â”Š1880â”Š    dir: string;
+â”Š    â”Š1881â”Š    /**

+â”Š    â”Š1893â”Š  }
+â”Š    â”Š1894â”Š
+â”Š    â”Š1895â”Š  /**

+â”Š    â”Š1897â”Š   * When multiple slashes are found, they're replaced by a single one; when the path contains a trailing slash, it is preserved. On Windows backslashes are used.
+â”Š    â”Š1898â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1899â”Š   * @param p string path to normalize.
+â”Š    â”Š1900â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1901â”Š  export function normalize(p: string): string;
+â”Š    â”Š1902â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1903â”Š   * Join all arguments together and normalize the resulting path.
+â”Š    â”Š1904â”Š   * Arguments must be strings. In v0.8, non-string arguments were silently ignored. In v0.10 and up, an exception is thrown.
+â”Š    â”Š1905â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1906â”Š   * @param paths string paths to join.
+â”Š    â”Š1907â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1908â”Š  export function join(...paths: string[]): string;
+â”Š    â”Š1909â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1910â”Š   * The right-most parameter is considered {to}.  Other parameters are considered an array of {from}.
+â”Š    â”Š1911â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1912â”Š   * Starting from leftmost {from} paramter, resolves {to} to an absolute path.
+â”Š    â”Š1913â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1914â”Š   * If {to} isn't already absolute, {from} arguments are prepended in right to left order, until an absolute path is found. If after using all {from} paths still no absolute path is found, the current working directory is used as well. The resulting path is normalized, and trailing slashes are removed unless the path gets resolved to the root directory.
+â”Š    â”Š1915â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1916â”Š   * @param pathSegments string paths to join.  Non-string arguments are ignored.
+â”Š    â”Š1917â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1918â”Š  export function resolve(...pathSegments: string[]): string;
+â”Š    â”Š1919â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1920â”Š   * Determines whether {path} is an absolute path. An absolute path will always resolve to the same location, regardless of the working directory.
+â”Š    â”Š1921â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1922â”Š   * @param path path to test.
+â”Š    â”Š1923â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1924â”Š  export function isAbsolute(path: string): boolean;
+â”Š    â”Š1925â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1926â”Š   * Solve the relative path from {from} to {to}.
+â”Š    â”Š1927â”Š   * At times we have two absolute paths, and we need to derive the relative path from one to the other. This is actually the reverse transform of path.resolve.
+â”Š    â”Š1928â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1929â”Š   * @param from
+â”Š    â”Š1930â”Š   * @param to
+â”Š    â”Š1931â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1932â”Š  export function relative(from: string, to: string): string;
+â”Š    â”Š1933â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1934â”Š   * Return the directory name of a path. Similar to the Unix dirname command.
+â”Š    â”Š1935â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1936â”Š   * @param p the path to evaluate.
+â”Š    â”Š1937â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1938â”Š  export function dirname(p: string): string;
+â”Š    â”Š1939â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1940â”Š   * Return the last portion of a path. Similar to the Unix basename command.
+â”Š    â”Š1941â”Š   * Often used to extract the file name from a fully qualified path.
+â”Š    â”Š1942â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1943â”Š   * @param p the path to evaluate.
+â”Š    â”Š1944â”Š   * @param ext optionally, an extension to remove from the result.
+â”Š    â”Š1945â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1946â”Š  export function basename(p: string, ext?: string): string;
+â”Š    â”Š1947â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1948â”Š   * Return the extension of the path, from the last '.' to end of string in the last portion of the path.
+â”Š    â”Š1949â”Š   * If there is no '.' in the last portion of the path or the first character of it is '.', then it returns an empty string
+â”Š    â”Š1950â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1951â”Š   * @param p the path to evaluate.
+â”Š    â”Š1952â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1953â”Š  export function extname(p: string): string;
+â”Š    â”Š1954â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1955â”Š   * The platform-specific file separator. '\\' or '/'.
+â”Š    â”Š1956â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1957â”Š  export var sep: string;
+â”Š    â”Š1958â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1959â”Š   * The platform-specific file delimiter. ';' or ':'.
+â”Š    â”Š1960â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1961â”Š  export var delimiter: string;
+â”Š    â”Š1962â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1963â”Š   * Returns an object from a path string - the opposite of format().
+â”Š    â”Š1964â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1965â”Š   * @param pathString path to evaluate.
+â”Š    â”Š1966â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1967â”Š  export function parse(pathString: string): ParsedPath;
+â”Š    â”Š1968â”Š  /**
+â”Š    â”Š1969â”Š   * Returns a path string from an object - the opposite of parse().
+â”Š    â”Š1970â”Š   *
+â”Š    â”Š1971â”Š   * @param pathString path to evaluate.
+â”Š    â”Š1972â”Š   */
+â”Š    â”Š1973â”Š  export function format(pathObject: ParsedPath): string;

```diff
+â”Š   â”Š149â”Š

+â”Š   â”Š152â”Š   * Wraps a function in a proxy function. All calls will
```

And run the following command which will install the declarations defined in the configuration files we've just added:

    $ typings install

By now if will you run the app you will receive warning notifications by the TypeScript compiler. This is caused due to our app not being fully migrated to TypeScript. Once you finish the upgrading process and your app is purely based on Angular2 with proper declarations you shall receive no warnings.

Now that the compiler is ready we will start by switching our entry file into TypeScript:

[{]: <helper> (diff_step 23.4)

[}]: #

Not only we changed the extension of the file, but we also made some adjustments to its content. All Angular1 modules registrations are now manually invoked, due to dependency on the upgrade who's gonna take part further in this tutorial. In addition, the way we import the `angular` library have changed.

Before:

```js
import angular from 'angular';
```

After:

```js
import * as angular from 'angular';
```

Now we gonna go through a component transformation. We will start with the Socially component since it is the root component of our app. We will first change the way we import Angular-related libraries, just like demonstrated above:

[{]: <helper> (diff_step 23.5)

```diff
 â”Š28â”Š41â”Š  "devDependencies": {
 â”Š29â”Š42â”Š    "angular-mocks": "^1.5.3"
```
[}]: #

Raw commands are listed below:

    $ npm install --save @angular/common
    $ npm install --save @angular/compiler
    $ npm install --save @angular/core
    $ npm install --save @angular/forms
    $ npm install --save @angular/platform-browser
    $ npm install --save @angular/platform-browser-dynamic
    $ npm install --save @angular/upgrade
    $ npm install --save angular2-meteor
    $ npm install --save angular2-meteor-polyfills
    $ npm install --save es6-shim
    $ npm install --save reflect-metadata
    $ npm install --save rxjs
    $ npm install --save underscore
    $ npm install --save zone.js

> `angular2-meteor-polyfills` will load `rxjs`, `reflect-metadata` and `zone.js` in their chronological order.

Now will start replacing our Angular1 components with Angular2 components, and it would be helpful if we could just do it gradually and not all at once, one component at a time. This is where the [Upgrade Adapter]([Upgrade Adapter](https://angular.io/docs/ts/latest/guide/upgrade.html) kicks in. The adapter will give us the ability to downgrade Angular2 so they can be registered to Angular1 modules, and upgrade Angular1 components so they can be registered to Angular2 modules, thereby we can have a hybrid app. Let's get into business by initializing a new instance of the `UpgradeAdapter` and passing it as an argument to each module registration:

[{]: <helper> (diff_step 23.10)

## Filters to Pipes

Angular1 filters have the same functionality as Angular2 pipes. Further details about the relation between filters pipes can be found in [Angular's docs](https://angular.io/docs/ts/latest/cookbook/a1-a2-quick-reference.html#!#filters-pipes). Filters should be registered to Angular1 modules as normal and pipes should be registered to Angular2 modules, so even though they are almost identical they will have to be duplicated for now.

We will start with the `displayName` pipe. This is how it should look like, and after we create a pipe it should be declared our app's Angular2 module:

[{]: <helper> (diff_step 23.12)
#### Step 23.12: Create displayNamePipe based on displayNameFilter

```diff
 â”Š29â”Š29â”Šimport { registerSocially, SociallyNg1Module } from '../imports/ui/components/socially/socially';
+â”Š  â”Š30â”Šimport { DisplayNamePipe } from '../imports/ui/filters/displayNamePipe';
```

The key concepts of this convertion are:

* import Pipe decorator.
* change name to *displayName*.
* move a function to be a class with `transform` method.
* remove everything related to Angular1.

## Using Material2

Indeed, We can also move our app's design stracture to Angular2 and reserve the API. Let's install the necessary packages

[{]: <helper> (diff_step 23.34)
#### Step 23.34: Install material2

##### Changed package.json
```diff
@@ -10,6 +10,7 @@
 â”Š10â”Š10â”Š    "@angular/compiler": "^2.1.0",

 â”Š12â”Š12â”Š    "@angular/forms": "^2.1.0",
+â”Š  â”Š13â”Š    "@angular/material": "^2.0.0-alpha.9-3",
 â”Š13â”Š14â”Š    "@angular/platform-browser": "^2.1.0",
 â”Š14â”Š15â”Š    "@angular/platform-browser-dynamic": "^2.1.0",
 â”Š15â”Š16â”Š    "@angular/upgrade": "^2.1.0",
```
[}]: #

Raw commands are listed below:

    $ npm install --save @angular/material

We now have `md-checkbox`, `md-button` and `md-input` available for us. But will first need to declare those:

The upgrading process for Socially might take a while and can be done in many different ways, but hopefully you got the concept. If your'e not familiar with Angular2-Metoer the following [tutorial](/tutorials/socially/angular2/bootstrapping) might come in handy.
